<div id="review_714438934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/714438934" />
    <a title="Sharon Bolton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6225577-sharon-bolton"><img alt="Sharon Bolton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442481009p2/6225577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/714438934?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Bolton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Bolton" href="/user/show/6225577-sharon-bolton">Sharon Bolton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780593064955" href="/book/show/14781675-i-am-pilgrim">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer714438934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11849548310200996291">‘The chemical flood hit his limbs – he realized with a wild rage that nothing could stop it now – and he saw his car keys fall from the jelly that used to be his hands.’ <br/><br/>I looked forward to this book for months and finished it in about four days which, when you consider it is nearly 800 pages long, says something about its pace. At the end of all that, I’m really not sure how to begin to review it. <br/><br/>Given everything I’d been led to expect, this much-hyped book started, for me, rather surprisingly</span>
  <span id="freeText11849548310200996291" style="display:none">‘The chemical flood hit his limbs – he realized with a wild rage that nothing could stop it now – and he saw his car keys fall from the jelly that used to be his hands.’ <br /><br />I looked forward to this book for months and finished it in about four days which, when you consider it is nearly 800 pages long, says something about its pace. At the end of all that, I’m really not sure how to begin to review it. <br /><br />Given everything I’d been led to expect, this much-hyped book started, for me, rather surprisingly quietly. A baffling murder scene in a run-down New York hostel brings together our hero, Pilgrim, and the NYPD copper, Ben Bradley, who eventually becomes Pilgrim’s side-kick and one of the most likeable characters of the book. It was interesting enough, well-written enough to hold my attention, but not the epic, race against time, most thrilling thriller ever written I’d been hoping for. <br /><br />It gets there – Oh, my, but it get’s there – it just doesn’t do it fast. There is a lot of backstory to get through before we can really get to grips with the main point of the book which, essentially, is a dual played out in a race against time, a clash of the Titans with not a moment to spare, a fight to the death between the two single strongest warriors of our age. Pilgrim and Saracen. <br /><br />Pilgrim is a member of the United States 'Department' - a kind of Military police for the CIA - staffed with people so deniable that even the Department's existence is kept secret. Pilgrim has risen through the shadowy ranks until he’s sent out to Turkey to discover all he can about a man who seems to be planning a massive bio-terror attack. <br /><br />It turns out to be the worst bio-terror attack imaginable: engineered smallpox that will devastate the world's population, starting with that of the United States. <br /><br />Saracen is a native of Saudi Arabia who, as a young boy saw his father publicly beheaded by the Saudi government. He and his family are forced to flee their home, he sees his beloved mother becoming increasingly westernized (corrupt) and eventually grows up to become one of the most trusted warriors of the Mujahedeen. The plot to annihilate America is his alone and he carries it out with a ruthless, terrifying brilliance. <br /><br />This book probably isn’t for everyone. Its length will put off some, as might the considerable amount of back story that needs to be absorbed in order to fully understand our two main characters. It has been described as both bigoted and racist, charges I wouldn’t accept, but I can understand why some people might be offended. On the other hand, it’s clever, brave, ambitious, fast-paced (towards the end I had to keep putting it down, I was genuinely afraid I might hyper-ventilate) original, brutal (one scene in particular I had to skip) and quite possibly the best thriller I’ve ever read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11849548310200996291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer105438444162613332">Astonishing. 700 pages of brilliance. A spy thriller that is so much more than that. It takes us, the lead characters and the author on a series of journeys, populated by 'real' people, obsessed by their own lives, living their own experiences,influenced or merely observed by our leads.   <span id="freeText105438444162613332" style="display:none">Astonishing. 700 pages of brilliance. A spy thriller that is so much more than that. It takes us, the lead characters and the author on a series of journeys, populated by 'real' people, obsessed by their own lives, living their own experiences,influenced or merely observed by our leads. It's a twisty path, covering so many countries, sometimes leading to tears, admiration, horror or to tremendous shocks and revelations. So many stories in one. This is indeed a storytelling pilgrimage. Every page had me riveted. I am so sorry to have finished it!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_883155928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/883155928" />
    <a title="Brandon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon"><img alt="Brandon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603283104p2/3214163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/883155928?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandon" href="/user/show/3214163-brandon">Brandon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=arc-reviews">arc-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3214163-brandon?shelf=2014">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer883155928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11633524104609634192">Pilgrim is the code-name for one of the world’s foremost authorities in forensic investigation. Spending his entire career employed by a secret division of the US government, Pilgrim rode off into the sunset by putting a lifetime of knowledge into what would become the definitive text on forensic crime scene investigation. But what happens when someone uses Pilgrim’s book as a manual for committing the perfect crime?<br/><br/><b>I received a free copy from Simon & Schuster in exchange for an honest review.</b><br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText11633524104609634192" style="display:none">Pilgrim is the code-name for one of the world’s foremost authorities in forensic investigation. Spending his entire career employed by a secret division of the US government, Pilgrim rode off into the sunset by putting a lifetime of knowledge into what would become the definitive text on forensic crime scene investigation. But what happens when someone uses Pilgrim’s book as a manual for committing the perfect crime?<br /><br /><b>I received a free copy from Simon &amp; Schuster in exchange for an honest review.</b><br /><br />The scope of Terry Hayes’ I Am Pilgrim is much larger than I initially expected. This tightly constructed, well researched thriller takes us around the world and into the lives of two very driven men on opposite sides of the spectrum. What begins as a squeaky clean murder scene expands into a global manhunt with the fate of the Western world hanging in the balance.<br /><br />When I first heard the synopsis, I instantly associated it with a Jack Bauer adventure. I expected a macho superspy loaded up with overflowing bravado with a penchant for kicking terrorist ass. Luckily for us, the author is ambitious enough to take a 600 page novel and really give it some backbone. The character development is top-notch and when both adversaries finally do meet, the groundwork has been laid perfectly to support such a high stakes battle.<br /><br />Without giving anything away, make sure you keep an eye on your pulse as the novel draws to a close. Despite all the work and all the room Hayes allotted himself to draw out the conclusion given the page count, he leaves it for the last thirty pages or so. That means that the storytelling is flying with white knuckle speed as Pilgrim tries to stop a global apocalypse. Great stuff.<br /><br />Supposedly this is the first in a series and while I’m up for revisiting the character, I would have been fine with this existing as a stand-alone novel – it’s that strong. If you’re a fan of blockbuster movies, this is one of those rare instances when a book can perfectly capture that feeling. Read with popcorn.<br /><br />Also posted @ <a href="http://everyreadthing.com/2014/04/09/i-am-pilgrim/" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Read Thing</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11633524104609634192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1523728677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523728677" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523728677?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552160964" href="/book/show/18395043-i-am-pilgrim">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=mystery-crime-thriller">mystery-crime-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=australian-author">australian-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=award-win-listed">award-win-listed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=dnf-abandoned">dnf-abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=chcc-library">chcc-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523728677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5384624411083082414"><b>3★<br/>“Due to my former work, I had more enemies than I cared to think about and I didn’t want to start my car engine one morning and end up as a handful of cosmic dust running rings around the moon.”</b><br/><br/>I should have liked this book. I should have enjoyed the plot and the characters. And I did, for a while. I began with the audio but started speeding it up as it seemed to be dragging. There were also some grisly details about killings and forensic investigation.<br/><br/>So I switched to reading a library versio</span>
  <span id="freeText5384624411083082414" style="display:none"><b>3★<br />“Due to my former work, I had more enemies than I cared to think about and I didn’t want to start my car engine one morning and end up as a handful of cosmic dust running rings around the moon.”</b><br /><br />I should have liked this book. I should have enjoyed the plot and the characters. And I did, for a while. I began with the audio but started speeding it up as it seemed to be dragging. There were also some grisly details about killings and forensic investigation.<br /><br />So I switched to reading a library version available for only an hour at a time online (and that was enough). At least I could pace myself and skim some of the worst stuff. In the beginning, I liked the main character and the story, how he was recruited into an elite government agency <b>“which worked so deep in shadow that only a handful of people knew of our existence . . .established by Jack Kennedy in the early months of his administration”.</b><br /><br />He begins as so many lone wolves do, as an only child whose father walked out before he was born and whose mother was murdered. Well, they don’t all have murdered mothers, but a lot of them are orphaned young. He was adopted by a wealthy couple and had the best of everything, except that the Mrs didn’t want him.<br /><br />We see him track down a powerful family of drug-dealers and arrange a hit. Later, the story turns to a young Saudi boy whose father has been beheaded in another gruesome episode. At one point, our main character says. <b>“Though no one will ever know for sure, I imagine that – mentally – he was being torn in two. . . ”</b> “He” is now referred to as the Saracen.<br /><br />I don’t know exactly where I noticed that the point of view was changing. Sometimes, the main character is narrating in the first person, sometimes it’s third person omniscient, where you have an outside storyteller, and then it goes back to our first person’s observations of what he thinks is happening.<br /><br />Our narrator, the main character, says again, that <b>“having seen all the secret evidence and, as I mentioned earlier, knowing more about him than anyone on earth, I am probably in the best position to say what happened up in the high mountains – an area which, despite the Saracen’s constant prayer rituals, must have given an entirely new meaning to the germ <i>‘godforsaken’.</i> <br /><br />Even though the tribesmen had mufflled their ponies well, the Saracen knew that they were there. Four days earlier, he had arrived and set up camp in the observation post’s old bunkhouse, blasted deep into the rock, and it was inside the cave that he awoke with a start. It was either his battlefield intuition or the restless movement of his horses that told him that he was no longer alone on the mountain.”</b><br /><br />So many people have loved this book, that I kept telling myself to just go along for the ride and enjoy the story. I gave up on the audio, although the narrator was fine – no complaints there. I just didn’t want some of those scenes echoing in my head quite so strongly.<br /><br />After about a third of the way through, I completely lost interest. I could see what the Saracen intended, but I couldn’t get past the fact that somehow I was privy to his innermost thoughts although I think I’m being told the story by the main character. It took me that much of the book to realise what my problem was, and it is obviously only my problem, or it wouldn’t be so popular, particularly for such a long read.<br /><br />So I apologise to all mystery lovers for my lack of enthusiasm, but maybe this was the wrong choice for right now. <br /><br />Moving right along . . .</span>
  <a data-text-id="5384624411083082414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O6dUWUqwJXMzqVcTfsTTRVuU1EK2Y+tpI1UKDnEuyZQBgT2L8e7sG5SC43KJMdmajcszinjuZQ54K0y/vG07Dg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YWUoVQESPrsyQxwkC9y56RAXxCEq1ZZgVTIbbvDbi0dbQ0GHukz305VoqEX8KbM2xkgj6eRYGAcOTF3fPZh53Q==')})
  }

Shantaram is narrated by Lin, an escaped convict with a false passport who flees maximum security prison in Australia for the teeming streets of a city where he can disappear.\n\nAccompanied by his guide and faithful friend, Prabaker, the two enter Bombay\'s hidden society of beggars and gangsters, prostitutes and holy men, soldiers and actors, and Indians and exiles from other countries, who seek in this remarkable place what they cannot find elsewhere.\n\nAs a hunted man without a home, family, or identity, Lin searches for love and meaning while running a clinic in one of the city\'s poorest slums, and serving his apprenticeship in the dark arts of the Bombay mafia. The search leads him to war, prison torture, murder, and a series of enigmatic and bloody betrayals. The keys to unlock the mysteries and intrigues that bind Lin are held by two people. <span id="freeTextContainer13403168570093404039">Terry Hayes began his career as a journalist for The Sydney Morning Herald, when as foreign correspondent in the US he covered Watergate and President Nixon's resignation, among many major international stories. He then went on to become a successful screenwriter, having written the screenplays for Mad Max 2, Dead Calm, Bangkok Hilton, Payback and From Hell. He lives in Sydney with his wife and fo</span>
  <span id="freeText13403168570093404039" style="display:none">Terry Hayes began his career as a journalist for The Sydney Morning Herald, when as foreign correspondent in the US he covered Watergate and President Nixon's resignation, among many major international stories. He then went on to become a successful screenwriter, having written the screenplays for Mad Max 2, Dead Calm, Bangkok Hilton, Payback and From Hell. He lives in Sydney with his wife and four children. </span>
